Report of the Administrative

In the year 2015, an income of Rs. 113.72 million was
generated through the operational activities of the
Authority and the overall income was Rs. 125.72 million. 1n
comparison to operational income in the year 2014 which
amounted to Rs. 121.41 million, the operational income
has posted a growth of 101%. The overall expenditure
in the year 2014 was Rs. 111.9 million and in comparison
the overall expenditure in 2015 was Rs. 97.4 million
during. The net post tax profit in the year 2015 was Rs
21.96 million and significantly this was the highest profit
recorded during the period from the year 2003 to date.

This increase in the income can be attributable to the
following factors.

© Notable increase in the Construction of new

condominium properties

© Increase in the Construction of Condominium
properties by both the state and private sectors in the
year 2015.

© Arrival of foreign investors for the construction of large
scale mix condominium properties in Colombo City.

Issuance of initial clearance for the
construction of condominium properties

With a view to minimizing recurrent problems such as
the furnishing the condominium plan to the Authority
after the construction of the condominium property
and inadequate provision of Common amenities
in certain constructions, it has been decided that
initial clearance instructions should be sought from
this Authority. Accordingly, initial clearance was
granted to 98 condominium properties proposed to
be constructed in the year 2014 and 106 clearance
letters were issued in the year 2015. These clearance
instructions served as guidance to property developers
in the construction activities.

Issuance of Condominium Certificates

One of the key regulatory responsibilities of this
Authority is to ensure that common amenities and
Common elements are available in the condominium
properties constructed by the public or private sector for
the benefit and welfare of the residents. As a result of
these condominium certificates, the unit owners of the
property have undisturbed possession of the Common
amenities and common elements. The certificates have
also contributed to prevent the registration of property
on forged documents and the delay in disposing the
ownership after having obtained money through sales
agreement.

Further, the issuance of this certificate has assured
the conformity with construction standards, proper
provision of utilities such as insurance schemes,

water, electricity while also making it possible to
exert pressure on the property developer.

The income generated through the issuance of
condominium certificates is the main source of income of
the Authority. From 2005, the Authority has issued 985
such certificates. Although 114 certificates were targeted
in the year 2015, the Authority received applications for
81 certificates.

Details of certificates issued by the Authority during the
period from 2012 to 2014 are tabulated below.

Annual       Progress
Targets
Financial (Rs Mn)      82.6              27.17
2013
Physical            112               66
Financial (Rs Mn)      29.425           94.16
2014
Physical           75                110
Financial (Rs Mn)      108.554          78.39
2015
Physical            114               81

Of the applications forwarded in the year 2014 seeking
to obtain condominium certificates, certificates were not
issued in respect of 59 of them owing to the non -issue
of certificate of compliance, not granting deeds and other
shortcomings.

A new trend in the construction of condominium property
has emerged with then entry 0 foreign investors into the
condominium sector in 2014.

An increasing trend in the construction of properties is
witnessed also due to the construction of Condominium
properties by the Urban Development Authority for
resettling tenement settlersand the construction of 50,000
houses under the new programme of the government.

Nearly 80 buildings constructed by the private sector
are unable to apply for the certification of the Authority
on account of being unable to obtain certificates of
compliance. There are 63 such properties of the National
Housing Development Authority as well. In order to
address this issue, the Authority as the regulator of
the sector, has obtained the approval of the Cabinet of
Ministers to amend the Apartment Ownership Act No 04
of 1999 and the relevant amendments have been referred
to the Legal Draughtsman and the relevant draft bill is
now under examination.

Further, a Bill introducing amendments to the
Condominium Management Authority Act No.10 of
1973 incorporating provisions making it mandatory
to obtain the provisional certificate of the Authority
before the construction of any condominium property
has received the approval of the Cabinet and referred
to the Legal Draftsman for drafting the bill.

Report of the Administrative

Establishing, registering and actively
maintaining Management Corporations

Though a property with private ownership is maintained by
the owners of such property, the maintenance of common
elements and common amenities in a condominium
property with shared ownership cannot be maintained
by any single individual and as such all those who share
these common elements and common amenities band
together to constitute management corporations which
are the legal structure for their administration.

From the year 2005 up to now, the authority has
constituted management Corporations in 833
condominium properties.

The progress achieved in establishing Management
Corporations by the Authority from 2013 up to 31.12.2015
is summarized in the following table.

Registration of management corporations and
committees/ renewal of registration /reactivating
dormant management corporations

tivating dormant

2015     64      50       539        397     1225 | 891

However, the following difficulties were experienced
in establishing management corporations

© Lack of understanding among property owners
regarding the importance of the Management
Corporation for maintaining property

© Lack of interest among residents of the apartment
housing schemes constructed by the government
agencies such as the Urban Development Authority for
the establishment of management corporations

© Owners of condominium property constructed by the
private sector not residing permanently in them

© Lassitude of owners to be involved in maintenance and
management activities under a voluntary basis due to
them being busy.

© Defaulting the payment of maintenance fees and other
residents not cooperating with the panel of office
bearers of the Management Corporation.

© Objections raised by the majority of occupants over
the high prevalence of unauthorized structures
in Condominium properties constructed by the
government.

Resolving disputes of Condominium

Property

The Authority has been vested with powers Common
Amenities Board Law No 10 of 1973 to intervene in the
event of disputes arising between the management of
the condominium property and the property owner or
between the residents and the owner or between the
owner and the buyer. Accordingly, when a complaint is
forwarded to the Authority in writing by those who have
entered into a sales agreement to purchase condominium
property or a resident, the Authority initiates necessary
action for its prompt resolution. Dispute which cannot be
resolved are referred to an investigation.

An investigation council has been set up for the resolution
of such disputes. The complaints received by the Council
can be categorized as follows according to their nature.

© Non granting of deeds to the residents since the
Condominium Plan cannot be registered despite the
lapse of a long period of time since the construction
and sale through a sales agreement.

© Construction in Violation of the approved building
plan; some property developers are unable to obtain
the certificate of compliance as they have executed
sales agreement after constructing only several floors.

© Not providing Common amenities and Common
elements in accordance with the approved plan

© Residents not paying the monthly maintenance fee to
the Management Corporation

© Erecting unauthorized structures and problems arising
in using Car parks and the public areas

In the year 2015, the Authority has taken measures to
resolve 60 complaints so received.

No of disputes resolved
2013                   130
2014                   75
2015                   60
Institutional mechanism to respond

positively to public grievances

© Upon receiving a complaint, forwarding a copy of the
complaint within 03 days to the respondent party and
obtaining observations within 14 days.

© Summoning the complainant and the respondent for

and concluding the inquiry

inquiry

Awareness Programmes

Educating Management Corporations, which is the legal
structure of residents of condominium property as
provided for by the Apartment Ownership Act No. 11 of
1973 and the Common Amenities Board Law No. 10 of
1973 and creating awareness among property developers
and other stakeholders on the administration and
maintenance of the property has to be carried out on a
regular basis.

Creating awareness among all stakeholders of the
condominium property is continually carried through
following steps.

Distributing 1,000 copies of “Condominium” journal.

© Conducting the annual general meetings and special
general meetings of Management Corporations under
the patronage of the officials of the Authority

Transferring Ownership of Tsunami
property Constructed under Tsunami
rehabilitation

The following facts came to light during the survey
conducted by the Authority on condominium property
constructed under Tsunami rehabilitation.

© The number of housing schemes constructed as fats is
39 and the number of housing units is 3749.

© The number of houses schemes constructed as twin
houses (joint) is 30 and the number of housing units
is 2064.

The Authority, having taken into account the fact that no
measures had been taken to dispose of the ownership
of these housing schemes, took this matter up with the
Ministry of Land and Land Development which owns
these lands and as a result such negotiations the approval
of the Cabinet of Ministers was secured to introduce
amendments to the Land Act to enable the transfer of
ownership of such lands and the drafting of relevant
regulations has been finalized by now and action has
been initiated to refer same to the Legal Draftsman's
Department.

For this purpose, the Authority conducted 02 workshops
in partnership with the Ministry of Land, the Land
Department and the Survey Department and the draft of
the necessary regulations was formulated. Action is also
being pursued in collaboration with the District Secretary,

Matara to award deeds in respect of two apartment
housing schemes in the Matara district.

Renovation of multi storeyed housing
schemes of government

As the residents of these housing schemes have failed to
properly maintain and administer their housing schemes
in good order, the National Housing Development
Authority has to spend public finances time and again
in huge amounts for their upkeep. Having studied this
Situation, action was taken to allocate funds from the
budgets for large scale renovations which the residents of
these schemes are unable to carry out on their own.

Boosted by this, a new trend and inclination towards the
establishment of management corporations has emerged.
Keeping the management corporation active will help
the residents to effectively carry out maintenance and
administration and will ultimately lead to the gradual
reduction of public funds spent on their maintenance.

12Paye


Report of the Administrative

Regulatory interventions of Condominium
Management Authority

Employing the aforementioned powers and provisions,
the Condominium Management Authority has been able
to execute the following very important services during
the year 2015.

© Measures were taken in the year 2015 to seek the
approval of the Cabinet to amend the Apartment
Ownership (Special Provisions) Act No 04 of 1994
enabling the registration of properties which had
been constructed several decades ago but which have
not been registered as a condominium property thus
preventing the handing over of their ownership to the
residents. The relevant draft which will enable to the
granting of deeds is in the process of being drafted
by the Legal Draftsman. More than 15,000 families
of housing schemes constructed by the public and
private sectors who have not been able to secure
deeds for their houses for more than 30-40 years will
be benefited from this programme.

Approval of the Cabinet of Ministers was also received
to appoint a panel of experts to amend the Common
Amenities Law No. 10 of 1973 and Apartment Ownership
Act No. 11 of 1973. Accordingly, amendments to the
Common Amenities Law No. 10 of 1973 were referred to
the Legal Draftsman to draft the relevant amendment bill.
The amended bill will address most of the practical issues
in the condominium sector and enable the Authority to
offer a wider range of services.

Meetings of the Board of Directors and
Meetings of Audit and Management
Committees

In the year 2015, 06 Board meetings were held and
decisions were taken as regards a host of important board
papers associated with the sector. 08 meetings of Audit
and Management Committee were held and 03 special
meetings of Audit and Management Committee were
held.

Having received the approval of the Cabinet of Ministers
for a cabinet memorandum submitted to secure Rs 143
million for the renovation of roads of 13 housing schemes
constructed by the Western Provincial Council, the roads
and storm water drain systems thereof were renovated
offering benefits to 1699 families.

Though the Condominium Management Authority was
established in the year 2003, the regulations pertaining to
the regulatory process had not been made even by 2014.
Hence, regulations were drafted and finalized in the year
2014 and arrangements have been made to gazette them
during the first quarter of 2016.

Restructuring Cadre

The cadre estimate and the promotion and recruitment
procedure of the Authority were approved by the
Department of Management Services in the year 2010.

Though the approved cadre of the Authority is 139, the
number of staff members by December 2015 was 102.
Action will be taken in 2016 to fill the existing vacancies.

Staff Training

Six employees of the Authority were made to participate
in local training programmes.

Efficiency Bar Examination

The efficiency bar examination was conducted in the
year 2015 for 15 officers of Management Assistant (Non
technical) MA 1-1-111 Grade. Arrangements have been
made to conduct the efficiency bar examination for the
rest of the staff during the first quarter of 2016.

A summary report of the Action Plan 2015 is attached
hereto.

Audit Report

Audit Report                                                              Answer of the Authority

12 Management's Responsibility regarding the Financial Statements

The preparation and fair presentation of
these financial statements in accordance
with Sri Lanka Accounting Standards
for public sector and deciding internal
controls to enable the preparation of
financial statements free from material
misstatements whether due to error
or fraud is the responsibility of the
management.

13 Responsibility Of the Auditor
My responsibility is to express an opinion
on these financial statements based on my
audit. | conducted my audit in accordance
with Sri Lanka auditing Standards
corresponding to international audit
standards of supreme audit institutions.
(ISSA! 1000-1810)
Those standards require that the audit
is planned and performed to secure
a reasonable assurance whether the
financial statements are free from material
misstatements.
An audit involves performing procedures
to obtain audit evidence about the
amounts and disclosures in the financial
statements. The procedures selected
depend on the auditor's judgment,
including the assessment of the risk of the
material misstatement of the consolidated
financial statements, whether due to fraud
or error. In making those risk assessments,
the auditor considers internal control
relevant to the Authority's preparation
and fair presentation of the consolidated
financial statements in order to design
audit procedures that are appropriate
in the circumstances, but not for the
purpose of expressing an opinion on the
effectiveness of the Authority's internal
control. An audit also includes evaluating
the appropriateness of Accounting Policies
used and the reasonableness of accounting
estimates made by management, as well
as evaluating the overall presentation of
the financial statements. Sub section (3)
and (4) of section 13 of the Finance Act No.
38 of 1971 give discretionary powers to the
Auditor General in determining the scope
and extent of the Audit.
| believe that the audit evidence | have
obtained is sufficient and appropriate to
provide a basis for my audit opinion

to 2015 after making adjustments for
employee remuneration, taxes paid to
the government and non- current assets
and compared to the contribution of Rs

4 Operational review

41 Performance

(a)As per the Common Amenities Board
Act No. 10 of 1973, the main objective
of the Authority is the management,
maintenance and control of Common
amenities of condominium properties
and offering guidance and assisting
the management corporation for the
proper execution of same and making
direct interventions when maintenance
is neglected. The disclosures from the
audit in respect of the performance of the
Authority are given below.

(i) Though the Authority should actively
maintain management corporations of
condominium properties, only 60% or
393 out of 666 management corporations
established by the Authority remained
active at the end of the year under review.

(a) (i) Even by now, 450 out of 860 management corporations
remain inactive. This is particularly evident in housing
schemes constructed by the public sector.

(ii) During the year under review, the physical | (ii) The delay in granting certificates of compliance by local

and financial progress in the issuance of
Condominium certificates was 71 % and
39% respectively and though it was planned
to insure 100 condominium properties
during the year, not a single property could
be insured during the year under review.

government authorities for the condominium properties
targeted for the year 2015 and condominium properties
constructed by the public sector not obtaining condominium
certificates were the main reasons for the decline in income

and physical values.

Further, establishment of new management corporations in
58 condominium properties and insuring them were carried
out as planned in the year 2015.

(iii) Though it

was targeted to issue
condominium registration certificates for
112 housing schemes constructed for the
tsunami affected people upon a provision
of Rs 10,000,000, the Authority had failed
to issue even a single certificate during the

year under review.

The Department of Lands is pursuing action to make new
regulations since there are no provisions in the Land Act to
transfer ownership of lands to tsunami property owners;
however this process is yet to be completed. But the transfer
of ownership of two tsunami condominium properties
constructed by the National Housing Development Authority
at Nupewela and Kammalwatta in Matara is being executed
by the NHDA in collaboration with this Authority.
Accordingly, Rs 1.86million out of the total provision of Rs 10
million allotted for this purpose had already been released
to the NHDA.

Though a provision of Rs. 80,000,000 from
the Treasury during the year under review
for finalizing the restoration activities at
Alokapura, Hilda and Samudra Shakthi
housing schemes, only Rs. 44,576,839
of that amount had been spent and the
physical progress of the project was less
than 50%.

The remaining renovation work of these three housing
schemes was Carried forward to 2016 and is due to be
completed during the current year.

Accordingly, the physical progress of the said project is 90%.

26 Page



Audit Report

Audit Report                                                              Answer of the Authority

Although,    regularizing    unregistered
government/    private    condominium
properties, appointing administrators
for dormant management corporations
and reporting to the Cabinet of Ministers
about properties unfit for living in order
to prevent any harm being caused to their
residents were to be carried out as per the
Action Plan during the year under review,
the Authority had carried out none of
them.

Since legal provisions have to be introduced for the
regularization of public and private condominium properties,
the Authority is pursuing action to amend the Apartment
Ownership (Special Provisions) Act No.04 of 1999 and
reenact the same and the relevant amendments are currently
in the process of being drafted by the Legal Draftsman's
Department.

Similarly, section (7) of the Act has provided for the
appointment of administrators for the dormant management
corporations only when the Authority is convinced that the
residents are unable to carry out maintenance activities in
the relevant property. However since no such requests were
received by the Authority during 2015, a need did not arise
to appoint such administrators.

the renovation of buildings of housing

buildings and the relevant report has also been submitted
to the Government Audit Division. The report has not

Indicators have not been prepared for the

relevant to strategies incorporated in the
Action Plan for the year 2015.

Measures have been taken to prepare performance

5.2 Budgetary documentary control

Since Variations ranging between 18 %
to 127% were observed when budgeted
income and expenses were Compared
with actual income and expenses, it Was
observed that the budget document had
not been used as an effective financial
control instrument.

Action will be taken to use the budget document as a control
instrument.

The Annual Report in respect of years 2012
and 2013 had not been tabled in Parliament
even by the end of the year under review.

Annual Report for 2012 has been tabled in Parliament and
the cabinet approval has been obtained for 2013 Annual
Report and is due to be tabled in Parliament.

Auditor's Responsibility

My responsibility is to express an opinion on these financial stutements bused on my
audit. | conducted my audit in accordance with Sri Lanka Auditing Standards
consistent with International Auditing Standards of Supreme Audit Institutions
([5$A! 1000 - 1810). Those Standards require that 1 comply with ethical
requirements and plan and perform the audit to oblain reasonable assurance about
Whether the nancial statements are fee fom material misstatements.

An audit involves performing procedures to obtain audit evidence about the amounts
and disclosures in the financial statements. The procedures selected depend on the
auditor's judgement, including the assessment of the risks of material misstatement of
the financial statements, whether due to fraud or mor, In making those risk
assessments, the audilor considers internal control relevant to the Authority's
preparation and fair presentation of the financial statements in onder Lo design audit
procedures that are appropriate 4 the Circumstances, but not for the purpose of
expressing an opinion on the effectiveness of the Authority's internal control. An
audit also includes evaluating the appropriateness of accounting policies used und the
reasonableness of accounting €stimates made by management, as well as evaluating
the owerall presentation of financial statements. Sub-sections (3) and (4) of Section 13
of the Finance Act, No.38 of 1971 give discretionary powers to the Auditor General to
determine the scope and extent of the audit.

1 believe that the audit evidence 1 have obtaincd is sufficient an appropriate to provide

a basis for my audit opinion.

3.          Financial Review

3,        Financial Results

According to the financial statements presented, the surplus of the Authority for the
year ended 31 December 2015 amounted to Rs.21,968.427 as compared with the
comesponding Surplus of Rs.10,449.154 for the preceding year, thus indicating un
improvement of Rs.11,519,273 in the financial results fur the year under review as
compared with the preceding year. The decrease of the operating expenditure of the
year under review by a sum of Rs.14476,438 had been the main reason for the above

improvement

An analysis of the financial results of the year under review and the (4 preceding
years revealed that, despite the deficits incurred in the years 2011 to 2013, surpluses
had been earned in the ycars 2014 and 2015. Even though the contribution of the
Authority, after the adjustment of employees' remuneration, the taxes paid to the
Government and the adjustment of tepreciation of non-current assets, had regularly
improved from the y€ar 2011 to the year 2015, the improvement in the year under
review, a5 Compared with the contribution of Rs.95,680,105 for the year 2014,
amounted only to 6 per cent.

34 Analytical Financial Review

The following observations are made.

{a) Even though the income from the issue of certificates for the condominium
properties had decreased by Rs.6,000,000 or 17 per cent, the service charges
income, as Conpared with the preceding year, had increased by Rs.15,700,000 or
990 per cent. As Such there was no Substantial change in the service charges

income for the year under review, as compared with the preceding year.

{b) The net assets of the Authority as at the end of the year under review amounted
Rs.33,509,521 as compared with the net assets of the preceding ycar amounting to
Rs.12,504,708. Accordingly an inrcase of Rs.21,004,813 in the net assets as

compared with the preceding year wus observed.

Financial Statement

01. Report ofthe Audit and Management

These accounting statements have been presented in compliance with generally accepted accounting principles and by selecting the Sri Lanka
public sector accounting policies endorsed by the public sector accounting standards committee, preparing accounting estimates in timely and
fair manner.

It is assured that measures have been taken to present fair financial statements by designing implementing and maintaining internal control rel-
evant to the preparation and fair presentation of financial statements that are free from material misstatement, whether due to fraud or error.

02      Accounting Policies

The accounting reports of the Authority have been presented with mutual interconnection between periods of time and on historic cost basis
in accordance with recognized accounting policies. Adjustments have been made towards inflationary factors that may affect the financial poli-
cies and the accounting reports have been prepared on accrual basis.

03       Location of the Authority

The Condominium Management Authority is located at the National Housing Development Authority at Sir Chittampalam A Gardianer
Mawatha, Colombo 02 and carries out regulatory duties in respect of condominium properties covering the entire island.

04       Legal nature of the Authority

In terms of the powers conferred under the Common Amenities Board (Amendment) Act No. 24 of 2003, it is the responsibility of the Authority
to establish management corporations for the maintenance administration and control of common elements and Common amenities in condo-

minium properties and to ensure that common facilities are provided so as to fulfill the needs of stakeholders.
05       Legislation relevant for the administration of operations of the Authority
Common Amenities Board (Amendment) Law No.10 of 1973

Common Amenities Board Act No. 46 of 1982

Common Amenities Board (Amendment) Act No 24 of 2003

Apartment Ownership Act No.11 of 1973

Apartment Ownership (Amendment) Act No. 45 of 1982

Apartment Ownership (Special Provisions) No.04 1999
Apartment Ownership (Amendment) Act 39 of 2003

06      The provisions for depreciation for fixed assets are calculated by using straight line basis from the
date of purchase to the date of sale as per the policy of the Authority

Motor vehicles                                             -25% 0n Cost
Office furniture                                            -20% 0n cost
Machinery and equipment                - 20% on cost
Office equipment                           - 20% on cost
Buildings                                     - 04% on cost

07 Gratuity
Allocations have been made in accounts for the value of the gratuity to be paid for employees who have completed a minimum period of

service of 05 years. Though the value of such allocation relevant to the year ended 31st December 2013 was Rs. 22,181,496.00, the value of
investment was only Rs. 3,524,226.00.

08 Stocks

Purchasing of stocks are valued at cost and adjusted in accounts and no profit percentage has been included in it.

45


Financial Statement

09        Income

Profit/loss accounts have been prepared on the basis of gross income.

10 Allocations for bad and doubtful debt
Allocations for bad and doubtful debt have been made on outcome on the basis of the age analysis of the debtors existing as at the end of the
year.

Years 0 -2               10%
Years 2-3              20%
Years 3-4              30%
Years 4-5               50%
Over 5 years           100%

11      Contingent liabilities

A case has been filed in the district court of Colombo under case number 53429/MR to recover Rs 807,187.50 due from Lanka Kate (Pvt) Ltd.
As there no contingent liabilities in respect of cases filed by or against the Authority, no allocations have been made in the accounts for that
purpose.

12       Lease Lend

A lease lend of Rs. 17,912,410 on 5 year repayment basis has been obtained from Bank of Ceylon for 03 cars and 01 cab purchased in the year
2012 and according to the accounts, a sum of Rs. 9,801,130.00 remains to be paid for the said lease lend.

13       EPF and ETF in arrears

As per the provisions of the Act, the cost of living allowance has not been taken into account in paying contributions of the employees of the
Authority for the Employees Provident Fund and the Employees’ Trust Fund from 2006.

Accordingly, action has been taken to allocate Rs. 18,705,202.92 in the accounts.
14       Capital projects

During the current year, an allocation of Rs. 106,014,695.05 for the emergency repairs of housing schemes constructed by the government and
Rs 1,576,649.50 for organizing awareness programmes to create awareness among residents of condominium properties and those connected
with the field and for publishing condominium publications and conducting seminars were made under the capital projects.

Accordingly, measures have been taken to allocate Rs. 61,088,017.55 received for the renovation of national housing schemes for the remain-
ing work.

15         Reserves

Total reserves                   - RS. 23,658,765.00
